<p><b>Lisa Raymond</b> (born August 10, 1973) is an American retired professional <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> player who has achieved notable success in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doubles_(tennis)" title="Doubles (tennis)">doubles tennis</a>. Raymond has 11 <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> titles to her name: 6 in women's doubles and 5 in mixed doubles. On June 12, 2000, she reached the world number one ranking in doubles. Her career high singles ranking was fifteenth in October 1997.</p>
<p>Earning more than US$9 million in prize money in her career, Raymond has reached the quarterfinals in singles at the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Open" title="Australian Open">Australian Open</a> and at <a href="/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon" title="The Championships, Wimbledon">Wimbledon</a>. Raymond, who plays right-handed, has wins over <a href="/wiki/Venus_Williams" title="Venus Williams">Venus Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arantxa_S%C3%A1nchez_Vicario" title="Arantxa Sánchez Vicario">Arantxa Sánchez Vicario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monica_Seles" title="Monica Seles">Monica Seles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Capriati" title="Jennifer Capriati">Jennifer Capriati</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martina_Hingis" title="Martina Hingis">Martina Hingis</a>. She is one of the few players to win a career <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)#Men.27s_doubles_2" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> in doubles. Among her doubles partners are <a href="/wiki/Lindsay_Davenport" title="Lindsay Davenport">Lindsay Davenport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martina_Navratilova" title="Martina Navratilova">Martina Navratilova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rennae_Stubbs" title="Rennae Stubbs">Rennae Stubbs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Stosur" title="Samantha Stosur">Samantha Stosur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kv%C4%9Bta_Peschke" title="Květa Peschke">Květa Peschke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cara_Black" title="Cara Black">Cara Black</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liezel_Huber" title="Liezel Huber">Liezel Huber</a>, among others. Raymond is also an Olympic medalist, winning the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tennis_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Mixed_Doubles" title="Tennis at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Mixed Doubles">bronze medal</a> in the mixed doubles competition at the <a href="/wiki/Tennis_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Tennis at the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> for the United States, partnering with <a href="/wiki/Mike_Bryan" title="Mike Bryan">Mike Bryan</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lisa_Raymond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lisa_Raymond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Raymond was born in <a href="/wiki/Norristown,_Pennsylvania" title="Norristown, Pennsylvania">Norristown, Pennsylvania</a>. She received an athletic scholarship to attend the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida" title="University of Florida">University of Florida</a> in Gainesville, Florida, where she played for coach <a href="/wiki/Andy_Brandi" title="Andy Brandi">Andy Brandi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators_women%27s_tennis" title="Florida Gators women's tennis">Florida Gators women's tennis</a> team. As a Gator, she won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA">NCAA</a> singles title in 1992 and 1993 and led the Gators to their first-ever NCAA national team championship in 1992. She was the first player to win all three collegiate Grand Slam titles in a single season (1992). She received the 1992 Volvo Rookie of the Year award, the 1992 <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tennis_Magazine" title="Tennis Magazine">Tennis Magazine</a></i> Collegiate Player of the Year award,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sonyericssonwtatour1_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-sonyericssonwtatour1-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> and twice received the <a href="/wiki/Honda_Sports_Award" title="Honda Sports Award">Honda Sports Award</a> for Tennis, recognizing her as the outstanding collegiate female tennis player of the year in 1991–92 and aqain in 1992–93.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a junior, Raymond won five U.S. National (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USTA" title="USTA">USTA</a>) singles and doubles titles, and she was ranked No.1 in the U.S. for players 18 and under in 1990. She was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Florida_Athletic_Hall_of_Fame_members" title="List of University of Florida Athletic Hall of Fame members">University of Florida Athletic Hall of Fame</a> as a "Gator Great" in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005.E2.80.932007">2005–2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lisa_Raymond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2005–2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Played the first half of the year with <a href="/wiki/Rennae_Stubbs" title="Rennae Stubbs">Rennae Stubbs</a> before beginning a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Stosur" title="Samantha Stosur">Samantha Stosur</a>, winning the US Open, her second doubles crown at Flushing Meadows, and the Season Ending Championships, also her second. Raymond and Stosur won six titles together and were named ITF World Doubles Champions of 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-itftennis1_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-itftennis1-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, Raymond and Stosur won ten titles including the French Open and their second Season Ending Championships. By winning the French Open, Lisa Raymond became only the 13th person in history to have won all four double Grand Slams. Finished the year as the co-holders of the number one spot. Won a WTA-leading 10 titles. Raymond and Stosur were again awarded by the ITF as World Doubles Chapmpions of 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-itftennis1_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-itftennis1-6">[6]</a></sup> They also received the WTA Team of the Year award for their achievents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sonyericssonwtatour1_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-sonyericssonwtatour1-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The year 2007 was a good one for Raymond and Stosur, with the pair winning five titles; also that year Lisa decided to retire from her singles career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> However, Stosur was diagnosed with a virus, forcing her to miss the second half of the season meaning Raymond had to play with various partners. Even though they only played half the season together, they had still qualified for the Season-ending Championships but could not compete.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008.E2.80.932009">2008–2009</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lisa_Raymond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2008–2009">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Raymond began 2008 playing with <a href="/wiki/Elena_Likhovtseva" title="Elena Likhovtseva">Elena Likhovtseva</a> with solid results but was cut short due to injury but then reunited with former partner <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Stosur" title="Samantha Stosur">Samantha Stosur</a> in May, after the latter's return from injury. They went on to reach the finals of Wimbledon and the US Open, losing both. Raymond also won titles in Memphis and New Haven.</p>
<p>In 2009, Raymond began a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Kv%C4%9Bta_Peschke" title="Květa Peschke">Květa Peschke</a>, where they reached four finals and two semi-finals before their year was cut short by an injury to Peschke, just before Wimbledon. Lisa played with different partners, winning one title, taking her tally to 68.</p>
<p>Raymond now considers her 2008–2009 seasons to be almost 'lost' due to a lack of drive in her fitness.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010">2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lisa_Raymond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Raymond started the year by reuniting with former partner Rennae Stubbs. They lost their first round in Sydney, before reaching the semi-finals of the Australian Open, as the number six seeds, losing to Venus and Serena Williams. Raymond also made the semi-finals of the Mixed doubles tournament. Raymond and Stubbs won the Aegon International against <a href="/wiki/Kv%C4%9Bta_Peschke" title="Květa Peschke">Květa Peschke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Katarina_Srebotnik" title="Katarina Srebotnik">Katarina Srebotnik</a> in the final 6–2 2–6 [13–11] Both Raymond and Stubbs qualified for the WTA Tour Championship at Doha and will face second seeds <a href="/wiki/Kv%C4%9Bta_Peschke" title="Květa Peschke">Květa Peschke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Katarina_Srebotnik" title="Katarina Srebotnik">Katarina Srebotnik</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011">2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lisa_Raymond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Raymond started the year by teaming up with Julia Görges but in April started a new partnership with Liezel Huber. Starting slowly, by May their results picked up with a quarter-final showing in Warsaw, semi-finals at Roland Garros and Birmingham, runners-up in Eastbourne and Stanford. They were also quarter-finalists at Wimbledon and Cincinnati. They won their first tournament in Toronto and then claimed the US Open and Tokyo, with a semi-final finish in Beijing which qualified them for the WTA Championships in Istanbul. Both have stated they want to continue their partnership in 2012 and hopefully play the London Olympics. Raymond has now won six women's Grand Slam double titles, three at the US Open, bringing her grand total to 9 (three in mixed) and 73 double titles in total.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012">2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lisa_Raymond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Raymond's first tournament of the year which was at Sydney she and her partner Huber were 2nd seeds. They got to the final where they were against top seeds Peschke and Srebotnik. The final was very close with the first 2 sets shared. In the deciding 3rd set the top seeds won 13-11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> In the Australian Open Raymond and Huber got to the quarter-finals without dropping a set but narrowly lost their quarter-final match to Mirza and Vesnina in the deciding 3rd set 7-6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Raymond and Huber won the next 4 tournaments which were in Paris, Doha, Dubai and Indian Wells. In Paris they were the top seeds. Groenefeld and martic were beaten in straight sets in the final. In Doha Raymond and Huber defeated Kops and Spears in the final in straight sets. In Dubai Raymond and Huber got revenge for their Australian Open defeat to Mirza and Vesnina by beating them in straight sets in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> At Indian Wells Raymond and Huber beat Mirza and Vesnina in straight sets again in the final. At Wimbledon Raymond and Huber were number 1 seeds but lost to eventual champions Serena and Venus Williams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Raymond's last tournament of the year was the Masters cup. Her partner in the doubles was Huber. They got to the semi-finals losing to Hlave and Hrade in straight sets.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013">2013</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lisa_Raymond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2013">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Raymond started the year ranked No. 6 in doubles. Her first tournament was with partner <a href="/wiki/Maria_Kirilenko" title="Maria Kirilenko">Maria Kirilenko</a> in <a href="/wiki/2013_Apia_International_Sydney_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2013 Apia International Sydney – Women's Doubles">Sydney</a>, where they were seeded 3rd. They beat <a href="/wiki/Marina_Erakovic" title="Marina Erakovic">Marina Erakovic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ekaterina_Makarova" title="Ekaterina Makarova">Ekaterina Makarova</a> in straight sets in the 1st round, but then lost in straight sets to <a href="/wiki/Darija_Jurak" title="Darija Jurak">Darija Jurak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Katalin_Marosi" title="Katalin Marosi">Katalin Marosi</a> in the 2nd round.</p>
<p>Next, Raymond and Kirilenko played at the <a href="/wiki/2013_Australian_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2013 Australian Open – Women's Doubles">Australian Open</a>, where they were seeded 3rd. They were beaten in straight sets in the 2nd round by the Australian duo of 16-year-old <a href="/wiki/Ashleigh_Barty" title="Ashleigh Barty">Ashleigh Barty</a> (who was playing with a wildcard) and <a href="/wiki/Casey_Dellacqua" title="Casey Dellacqua">Casey Dellacqua</a>, who later went on to reach the final. After the Australian Open, she dropped to No. 7, being overtaken in the rankings by her partner <a href="/wiki/Maria_Kirilenko" title="Maria Kirilenko">Kirilenko</a>.</p>
<p>In February, Raymond teamed up with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sam_Stosur" title="Sam Stosur">Sam Stosur</a> to play at the <a href="/wiki/2013_Qatar_Total_Open_%E2%80%93_Doubles" title="2013 Qatar Total Open – Doubles">Doha</a> tournament, where they were unseeded and beat 8th seeds <a href="/wiki/Bethanie_Mattek-Sands" title="Bethanie Mattek-Sands">Bethanie Mattek-Sands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sania_Mirza" title="Sania Mirza">Sania Mirza</a> in straight sets, then beat <a href="/wiki/Janette_Hus%C3%A1rov%C3%A1" title="Janette Husárová">Janette Husárová</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Shuai_(tennis)" title="Zhang Shuai (tennis)">Shuai Zhang</a> 2:1 sets, but lost in the quarter-finals against 3rd seeded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raquel_Kops-Jones" title="Raquel Kops-Jones">Raquel Kops-Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abigail_Spears" title="Abigail Spears">Abigail Spears</a> in straight sets.</p>
<p>Next, in March, Raymond played in <a href="/wiki/2013_Sony_Open_Tennis_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2013 Sony Open Tennis – Women's Doubles">Miami</a>, where she teamed up with British teenager <a href="/wiki/Laura_Robson" title="Laura Robson">Laura Robson</a> (who was playing with a wild card). They reached the semi-finals, where they beat 1st seeds and World #1 pair <a href="/wiki/Sara_Errani" title="Sara Errani">Errani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roberta_Vinci" title="Roberta Vinci">Vinci</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> in straight sets with the loss of just 3 games, but then lost in straight sets against 3rd seeds <a href="/wiki/Nadia_Petrova" title="Nadia Petrova">Nadia Petrova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Katarina_Srebotnik" title="Katarina Srebotnik">Katarina Srebotnik</a> in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> This partnership continued into the 2013 Wimbledon tournament.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014">2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lisa_Raymond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Raymond started the year ranked 42 in the doubles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> She reached the final of her first tournament of the year Hobart with Zhang Shuai as her partner. They narrowly lost to Monica Niculescu and Clara Zakopalová. In the Australian Open she partnered Hantu. They reached the 3rd round and got knocked out by Marka and Vesni. At Nurenberg she gets as far as semi-final with Huber as her Partner Huber. The same pair lose to eventual French Open champions Hsei and Peng in the 3rd round. At Wimbledon Raymond and Huber were seeded 15th but lost in the 2nd round. In the US Open Raymond temed up with King and they got to the 3rd round before losing to the eventual tournament winners Makarova and Vesnina. Raymonds best result in the mixed doubles was a 2nd round exit at the Australian Open with Fryst as her partner. In the French Open and US Open she lost in the 1st round with Peers and Lipsk respectively.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_finals">Major finals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lisa_Raymond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Major finals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lisa_Raymond&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">
